Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Thought:
  Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours.
  Jack finished two-thirds of the work.
  This means that only one-third of the work is left for Jill to do.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of what Jack can do.
  This means that Jill's rate of cleaning is (5/100)*1 = 1/20 of Jack's rate.
  Let's say it takes Jill 'x' hours to finish the remaining work.
  We can use the formula: Work = Rate * Time
  Jack's rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 1/20 of Jack's rate, which is (1/20)*(1/12) = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  Using the formula, we can set up an equation: (1/3) = (1/12)*(2/3) + (1/240)*x
  Solving for 'x', we get x = 8.
  Therefore, it takes Jill 8 hours to finish the remaining work.
  The answer is B: 8.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 70 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train is 'x' hours.
  Therefore, the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel back from the city by car is also 'x' hours.
  According to the question, Mr. Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to the city and return by car.
  Therefore, the total time taken by Mr. Sam = x + x = 2x (to go and return) + 17 (4 hours extra).
  If Mr. Sam had traveled by car in both ways, the total time taken would have been 2x - 4.
  We can solve for 'x' using these two equations.
  2x + 17 = 2x - 4
  17 = -4
  This equation is not possible, which means there is no valid solution.
  Therefore, the answer is "None of the Above".
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the time taken by train to reach the city is 'x' hours.
  Therefore, the time taken by car to return from the city is also 'x' hours.
  Total time taken by Mr. Sam = 17 hours
  If he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours.
  Therefore, the total time taken by train = 17 + 4 = 21 hours
  Total time taken by train to reach the city and return by car = x + x = 2x hours
  Total time taken by Mr. Sam = 21 hours
  Therefore, 2x = 21 => x = 10.5
  Time taken by car to return from the city = x = 10.5 hours
  Therefore, the total time taken by Mr. Sam if he had traveled by car in both ways = 2x = 2 * 10.5 = 21 hours
  The answer is D: 20 hrs.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the time taken to travel by train to the city is t1 and the time taken to travel by car to the city is t2.

  We also know that t1 - t2 = 4 (time difference when he goes both ways by train)
  Adding these two equations, we get 2t1 = 21, which gives us t1 = 10.5
  Substituting t1 in the first equation, we get t2 = 6.5
  The total time taken to travel by car in both ways would be 2t2 = 13
  Therefore, the answer is E: 13 hrs

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 71 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the diver brought x copper coins and y brass coins.
  The amount earned by bringing copper coins = 20x cents.
  The amount earned by bringing brass coins = 25y cents.
  The total amount earned by the diver = 340 cents.
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that she brought.
  We can use trial and error to solve this problem.
  Let's start with option A: 4 copper coins.
  The amount earned by bringing 4 copper coins = 20*4 = 80 cents.
  The remaining amount earned by bringing brass coins = 340 - 80 = 260 cents.
  The number of brass coins required to earn 260 cents = 260/25 = 10.4.
  This is not possible as the number of brass coins must be a whole number.
  Let's try option B: 3 copper coins.
  The amount earned by bringing 3 copper coins = 20*3 = 60 cents.
  The remaining amount earned by bringing brass coins = 340 - 60 = 280 cents.
  The number of brass coins required to earn 280 cents = 280/25 = 11.2.
  This is not possible as the number of brass coins must be a whole number.
  Let's try option C: 2 copper coins.
  The amount earned by bringing 2 copper coins = 20*2 = 40 cents.
  The remaining amount earned by bringing brass coins = 340 - 40 = 300 cents.
  The number of brass coins required to earn 300 cents = 300/25 = 12.
  This is possible as the number of brass coins is a whole number.
  Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 2.
  The answer is C: 2.

  D: 997
  E: 112

  If we subtract 495 from abc, we get cba.
  Therefore, abc - 495 = cba.
  Substituting a = 17 - b - c into the equation a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109 and simplifying, we get b^2 + 2bc + 2b - 34c + c^2 - 289 = 0.
  Rearranging, we get 2b^2 + 2bc + 2b - 34c + c^2 - 289 = b^2.
  Substituting b = 17 - c - a and a = 17 - b - c, we get 2(17 - c - b)^2 + 2(17 - c - b)c + 2(17 - c - b) - 34c + c^2 - 289 = (17 - c - b)^2.

  Solving for c using the quadratic formula, we get c = 8 or c = 5/3.
  Since c is an integer, we must have c = 8.

  Since a, b, and c are digits, we must have a, b ≤ 9.
  We can check that the only solution to a + b = 9 with a, b ≤ 9 is a = 1 and b = 8.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 74 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the side of the cube is 'a'.
  The diameter of the sphere will be equal to the side of the cube.
  The radius of the sphere, r = a/2.
  The volume of the cube = a³
  The volume of the sphere = (4/3)πr³ = (4/3)π(a/2)³ = (4/3)π(a³/8) = πa³/6
  The ratio of the volume of the cube to that of the sphere = a³ / (πa³/6) = 6/π
  Therefore, the answer is D: 6: π.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the edge of the cube is 'a'. 
  The volume of the cube is a³.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge of the cube, so the diameter of the sphere is also 'a'.
  The radius of the sphere is a/2.
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)π(r³) = (4/3)π(a/2)³ = (1/6)πa³.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is a³ : (1/6)πa³ = 6 : π.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 2: π.

  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is a³ : (1/6)πa³ = 6 : π.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 6: π.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 75 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to divide the 10 lime soda bottles into 2 groups of 5.
  The first group can be chosen in 10 choose 5 ways.
  The second group is determined once the first group is chosen.
  Therefore, the total number of ways to create these 2 groups is 10 choose 5.
  10 choose 5 = (10!)/((5!)(10-5)!) = 252.
  The answer is D: 252.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The first group can be formed in 10 choose 5 ways.
  The second group can be formed in 5 choose 5 ways (since there are only 5 bottles left).
  Therefore, the total number of ways to create these 2 groups is (10 choose 5) * (5 choose 5).
  We know that n choose k = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).
  Therefore, (10 choose 5) = 10! / (5! * 5!) = 252.
  Also, (5 choose 5) = 5! / (5! * 0!) = 1.
  Therefore, (10 choose 5) * (5 choose 5) = 252 * 1 = 252.
  The answer is D: 252.

  We have 10 bottles and we need to choose 5 for the first group, so n=10 and r=5.

  Therefore, the answer is D: 252.

Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let V be the number of files infected by a virus.
  Let W be the number of files infected by a worm.
  Let B be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  We know that V + W - B = 250 (all 250 files are infected by either a virus or a worm or both).
  We also know that W = 2.5B (the number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm).
  We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus. Therefore, V = 0.5(250) = 125.
  We can substitute V and W in terms of B to get B = 25 and W = 62.5.
  The number of files not infected by a worm is 250 - (W - B) = 250 - 37.5 = 212.5.
  The closest answer choice is E: 125.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:

  Let x be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  Then, the number of files infected only by a worm would be 2.5x.
  Let y be the number of files infected only by a virus.
  We know that the total number of files is 250.
  Therefore, we can write an equation: x + 2.5x + y = 250
  Simplifying the equation, we get 3.5x + y = 250
  We also know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus.
  This means that the number of files infected by a virus is 50% of 250, which is 125.
  Therefore, y = 125 - x
  Substituting y in the equation above, we get 3.5x + (125 - x) = 250
  Solving for x, we get x = 50
  Therefore, the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5x = 125
  The number of files NOT infected by a worm would be 250 - (x + 2.5x) = 250 - 3.5x
  Substituting x = 50, we get the number of files NOT infected by a worm is 75.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 75.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 77 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let CP be the cost price of the article.
  Profit % = 20%
  Selling price = Rs.360
  Selling price = Cost price + Profit
  360 = CP + (20/100)*CP
  360 = CP + 0.2CP
  360 = 1.2CP
  CP = 360/1.2
  CP = 300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
Action: Answer("B")

Thought:

So, (120/100)*x = 360

Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.

Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
- Let's call the number of newspapers ordered on Sunday "x".
- The number of newspapers ordered on the rest of the days of the week is then "x/2" since the hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week.
- The cost of the newspapers on Sunday is $4x, and the cost of the newspapers on the rest of the days of the week is $1(x/2) = $0.5x.
- The total cost of the newspapers is $210, so we can write an equation: $4x + $0.5x * 6 = $210 (since there are 6 days in the week that are not Sunday).
- Solving for x, we get x = 30.
- So the hotel orders 30 newspapers on Sunday and 15 newspapers on each of the other days.
- Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
- Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday.
- On Sunday, the hotel buys 2x newspapers.
- The hotel orders newspapers for 7 days in a week.
- The total cost of the newspapers for a week is $210.
- On Sunday, the hotel pays $4 per newspaper, and on the other days, it pays $1 per newspaper.
- Therefore, the equation that represents the total cost of the newspapers for a week can be written as follows: 
  4(2x) + 1(7x) = 210
- Solving the above equation, we get x = 15.
- So, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday.
- Therefore, the hotel buys a total of 15*6 = 90 newspapers from Monday to Saturday.
- On Sunday, the hotel buys 2x = 2*15 = 30 newspapers.
- Hence, the hotel buys a total of 90+30 = 120 newspapers in a week.
- To find how many newspapers the hotel buys on Monday, we need to subtract the number of newspapers bought on Sunday from the total number of newspapers bought from Monday to Sunday.
- Therefore, the hotel buys 120 - 30 = 90 newspapers on Monday.
- The answer is B: 30.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the time taken for Allen and Bob to meet for the second time be t.
  Let the distance travelled by Allen before they meet for the first time be x.
  Since they both meet for the second time, Allen would have travelled a distance of d-x+d.
  Bob would have travelled a distance of d+(d-x)+48.
  We can form an equation using the distance, speed and time formula for both Allen and Bob.
  Then we can solve for d.
Action: Answer("A")  144km
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the time taken by Allen to reach Y be t.
  Let the time taken by Bob to reach X be t1.
  Let the time taken by Allen to return to X be t2.
  Distance covered by Allen in t hours = 54t
  Distance covered by Bob in t1 hours = 78t1
  Distance covered by Allen in t2 hours = 54t2
  Total distance covered by Bob = 78t1 + d + 78t2
  Total distance covered by Allen = 54t + 54t2
  Bob covers 48 km more than Allen when they meet for the second time. Therefore,
  78t1 + d + 78t2 = 54t + 54t2 + 48
  78t1 + 78t2 - 54t2 = 54t + d + 48
  78(t1 + t2) - 54t2 = 54t + d + 48
  24(t1 + t2) = 54t + d + 48 + 54t2
  12(t1 + t2) = 27t + d/2 + 24t2
  Also, distance covered by Allen = distance covered by Bob
  54t + 54t2 = 78t1 + d + 78t2 - 48
  54t + 54t2 = 78(t1 + t2) + d - 48
  Substituting 54t + 54t2 from the above equation
  78(t1 + t2) + d - 48 = 12(t1 + t2) + d/2 + 24t2
  66(t1 + t2) = d/2 + 48 + 24t2
  33(t1 + t2) = d/4 + 24 + 12t2
  We know that the distance covered by Allen in t hours = 54t and the distance between X and Y is d.
  Therefore, 54t + 54t2 = d
  54(t + t2) = d
  Substituting d in the above equation
  54(t + t2) = 33(t1 + t2) + 24 + 12t2
  54t + 54t2 = 33t1 + 33t2 + 24 + 12t2
  54t + 42t2 = 33t1 + 24
  18t + 14t2 = 11t1 + 8
  We have three equations and three variables. We can solve for t, t1, and t2.
  Solving the equations, we get t = 4, t1 = 6, and t2 = 1.
  Therefore, d = 54(t + t2) = 54(4 + 1) = 270 km.
  The answer is A: 144 km.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the number of lilies on the lake can be represented by the function f(t) = 2^(t/2), where t is the number of days.
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, so f(60) = 2^(60/2) = 2^30 = N, where N is the number of water lilies on the lake after 60 days.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, we need to find the number of days it takes for the number of lilies to reach N = 2^30 starting from 64.
  That is, we need to solve the equation 2^(t/2) = 2^30 / 64 = 2^28.
  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get t/2 = 28, so t = 56.
  Therefore, it takes 56 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies if initially there were 64 water lilies on it.
  The answer is D: 53.
Action: Answer("D")

  If there is one water lily on the first day, then on the second day there will be 2 lilies, on the third day there will be 4 lilies, and so on.
  After x days, there will be 2^(x/2) lilies on the lake.
  We can set up an equation to solve for x: 2^(x/2) = 64 * 2^(60/2).
  Simplifying this equation, we get 2^(x/2) = 64 * 2^30, which is equivalent to 2^(x/2) = 2^36.
  Therefore, x/2 = 36, which means x = 72.
  Therefore, if initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, it will take 72 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours from City A to City B.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours from City B to City A.
  The total distance between the two cities is covered when the two trains meet.
  Let's assume that the two trains meet after x hours of Train N's departure from City B.
  Distance covered by Train M = Speed of Train M * Time = x + 2 hours
  Distance covered by Train N = Speed of Train N * Time = 3.5x hours
  Distance covered by Train M = Distance covered by Train N
  Therefore, x = 7/3 hours or 2 hours and 20 minutes after 7 am, which is 9:20 am.
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 9:20 am.
  The time taken for the two trains to cross each other is 2 hours and 20 minutes - 2 hours = 20 minutes.
  The answer is not one of the choices. 
  The closest answer is E: 55 min.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours (5 am to 9 am).
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours (7 am to 10:30 am).
  Let's assume that the two trains meet at time T after Train N has started.
  Train M has traveled for T-5 hours.
  Train N has traveled for 10:30-T hours.
  The total distance traveled by both trains is the same.
  Let's assume that the distance between City A and City B is D.
  The distance traveled by Train M is D.
  The distance traveled by Train N is also D.
  The speed of Train M is D/(T-5).
  The speed of Train N is D/(10:30-T).
  Equating the two speeds, we can solve for T.
  D/(T-5) = D/(10:30-T)
  T = 8:20 am
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 8:20 am.
  The time elapsed since Train N started is 1 hr 20 min.
  The time elapsed since Train M started is 3 hrs 20 min.
  The time elapsed between the departure of Train N and the crossing is 1 hr 20 min - 1 hr = 20 min.
  The answer is E: 55 min.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours from City A to City B.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours from City B to City A.
  Let's assume the trains cross each other 'x' hours after Train N leaves City B.
  In 'x' hours, Train M would have traveled for x + 4 hours.
  In 'x' hours, Train N would have traveled for 3.5 - x hours.
  The total distance traveled by both trains would be equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  Therefore, we can form the following equation: 
  Distance traveled by Train M + Distance traveled by Train N = Distance between City A and City B
  (x+4)M + (3.5-x)N = D
  where M and N are the speeds of Train M and Train N respectively, and D is the distance between City A and City B.
  We need to solve for 'x' to find the time when the trains cross each other.
  The answer is the time elapsed between 7 am (when Train N leaves City B) and the time when the trains cross each other.
  Let's solve for 'x'.
  (x+4)M + (3.5-x)N = D
  (x+4)M + (3.5-x)M = D  (since both trains have the same speed)
  7.5M + 0.5Mx = D
  0.5Mx = D - 7.5M
  x = (D - 7.5M) / 0.5M
  We know that M = Distance / Time = D / 4  (since Train M takes 4 hours to travel from City A to City B)
  Substituting M = D / 4 in the above equation, we get:
  x = (D - 7.5(D/4)) / (0.5(D/4))
  x = (D/2) / (D/8)
  x = 4
  Therefore, the trains cross each other 4 hours after Train N leaves City B, which is at 11 am.
  The time elapsed between 7 am and 11 am is 4 hours.
  Therefore, the answer is E: 55 min.

Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours from City A to City B.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours from City B to City A.
  The total time from when Train M leaves City A to when Train N reaches City A is 4 + 3.5 = 7.5 hours.
  The two trains cross each other when they have traveled a combined distance equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  Let's assume that the two trains cross each other x hours after Train M leaves City A.
  At the time of crossing, Train M would have traveled for x hours and Train N would have traveled for (x - 2) hours.
  The distance traveled by Train M = speed of Train M x time taken = s x x.
  The distance traveled by Train N = speed of Train N x time taken = s x (x - 2).
  The sum of the distances traveled by the two trains is equal to the distance between City A and City B.
  Therefore, s x x + s x (x - 2) = d, where d is the distance between City A and City B.
  Solving for x, we get x = d / (2s - s) = d / s.
  The time taken by the two trains to cross each other is x - 5 = d / s - 5.
  Therefore, the answer is (d / s) - 5.
Action: Answer("B")
Votes: E, E, E, N, E, A, B, A, E, B
Agent Answer: E
Correct Answer: D

Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The average weight of the 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons.
  Therefore, the total weight of the 10 vehicles is 10 x 12.2 = 122 tons.
  After adding the new truck, the average weight of the group increased by 2.6 tons.
  Let the weight of the new truck be x.
  Then, the new total weight of the 11 vehicles is (122 + x) tons.
  The new average weight of the 11 vehicles is (12.2 + 2.6) = 14.8 tons.
  So, we can set up the equation: (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Solving for x, we get x = 41.6
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 41.6 tons.

Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Thought:
- We have 10kg mixture with 30% sand and 70% clay.
- We want to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
- Let's assume that we need to remove x kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- The amount of sand in the new mixture will be (10 - x) * 0.3 + x = 0.5 * (10 - x)
- The amount of clay in the new mixture will be (10 - x) * 0.7 = 0.5 * (10 - x)
- Solving for x, we get x = 4.
- Therefore, we need to remove 4kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- Answer is A: 10/7

  Therefore, each person needs 1/8 of the total bottles of soda.
  Jill needs to buy 12/8 times the number of bottles she needed for 8 people.
  12/8 times 10 is 15.
  Therefore, Jill needs to buy 15 bottles of soda for a party in which 12 people are attending.
Action: Answer("E")

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the length and breadth of the rectangular plot be L and B.
  Given, perimeter of the plot = 2(L+B) = 340
  L + B = 170
  Let the width of the boundary be x.
  The length and breadth of the plot with the boundary will be (L+2x) and (B+2x).
  The area of the plot with the boundary will be (L+2x)(B+2x).
  The area of the plot without the boundary will be L*B.
  The area of the boundary will be the difference between the two areas.
  Area of the boundary = (L+2x)(B+2x) - L*B
                       = 2Lx + 2Bx + 4x^2
  Cost of gardening 1 square metre = 10
  Cost of gardening the boundary = Area of the boundary * 10
                                  = 10(2Lx + 2Bx + 4x^2)
                                  = 20(L+B)x + 40x^2
  Substituting L+B = 170, we get
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 20(170)x + 40x^2
                                  = 3400x + 40x^2
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-metre broad boundary, i.e., x=1.
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 3400(1) + 40(1)^2
                                  = 3440
  Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-metre broad boundary is 3440.
  The answer is C: 3440.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the length of the rectangular plot is l and the breadth is b.

  We also know that the cost of gardening 1 square meter is 10.
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot.
  The length of the boundary is l+2 and the breadth of the boundary is b+2.
  Therefore, the area of the boundary is (l+2)(b+2) - lb square meters.
  The cost of gardening the boundary is 10 times the area of the boundary.
  Substituting l+b=170, we can simplify the expression for the area of the boundary to 170+4 = 174 square meters.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the boundary is 10*174 = 1740.
  The answer is A: 3400.

  = 2(L+W+2)
  = 2(170+2)
  = 344
  Therefore, the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around a rectangular plot having a perimeter of 340 meters at the rate of 10 per square meter is 3440.

Question: The capacity of a tank of dimensions (8 m × 6 m × 2.5 m) is
Choices:
  A: 120 litres
  B: 1200 litres
  C: 12000 litres
  D: 120000 litres
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  The capacity of a tank is the amount of liquid it can hold.
  The dimensions of the tank are given as 8 m × 6 m × 2.5 m.
  To find the capacity of the tank, we need to find the volume of the tank.
  The volume of the tank is given by the formula length × width × height.
  Therefore, the volume of the tank is 8 m × 6 m × 2.5 m = 120 cubic meters.
  1 cubic meter = 1000 litres.
  Therefore, the capacity of the tank is 120 × 1000 = 120000 litres.
  The answer is D: 120000 litres.

Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
  Profit per kg of oranges = Selling price - Cost price = Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  Profit percentage = (Profit / Cost price) * 100
  Profit percentage = (2.50 / 5) * 100 = 50%
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450.
  The cost price of one kg of oranges is Rs. 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold the whole lot at Rs. 7.50 per kg.
  The selling price of 90 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50 x 90 = Rs. 675.
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = Rs. (675 - 450) = Rs. 225.
  Percentage gain = (Profit / Cost Price) x 100%
  Percentage gain = (225 / 450) x 100%
  Percentage gain = 50%
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.

  B: 26 days
  C: 27 days
  D: 28 days
  E: 29 days

  However, the frog can climb 1m each day, so on the 30th day, the frog will climb 1m and get out of the well.

Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?

  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume Joe's age as "J", Joe's sister's age as "S" and Joe's father's age as "F".
  We have two equations and two variables:
    J + S + F = 100   (Equation 1)
    J + (t-F) = F     (Equation 2)  (where t is the time in years for Joe to be as old as his father)
  From Equation 2, we get:
    J + t - F = F
    J + t = 2F
    t = 2F - J     (Equation 3)
  We have another equation based on the second condition:
    S + t = 2S     (Equation 4)  (where t is the time in years for Joe to be as old as his father and S is Joe's sister's age)
    t = S
  Substituting Equation 3 in Equation 4, we get:
    2F - J = S
    S = 2F - J     (Equation 5)
  Substituting Equation 5 in Equation 1, we get:
    J + (2F - J) + F = 100
    3F = 100
    F = 33.33 (approx) years
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is approximately 33.33 years.
  Since none of the answer choices match with this, the most likely answer is the closest one to 33.33, which is A: 45.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the amount Christopher gives to Jonathan is equal to the amount Jonathan gives to Christopher, then the total number of heads must be equal to the total number of tails.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on heads x times, then it landed on tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times, so he gave a total of 2x dollars.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher (20-x) times, so he gave a total of 3(20-x) dollars.
  Since they both won and lost the same amount, we can set up an equation:
  2x = 3(20-x)
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.
  Therefore, the coin landed on heads 12 times.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  For every flip, the difference between the amount Christopher gives and the amount Jonathan gives is $2 - $3 = -$1.
  If neither of them won or lost any amount, then they must have had an equal number of Heads and Tails.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, it landed on Tails (20 - x) times.
  The total amount that Christopher gave to Jonathan is 2x.
  The total amount that Jonathan gave to Christopher is 3(20 - x) = 60 - 3x.
  Since they did not win or lose any amount, then the total amount that Christopher gave to Jonathan must be equal to the total amount that Jonathan gave to Christopher.
  2x = 60 - 3x
  5x = 60
  x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let d be the distance between A and B.
  Let t1 be the time it takes for Kevin to reach B from A.
  Let t2 be the time it takes for Kevin to return from B to A.
  We know that Kevin drove at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B, and at a constant speed of 90 mph from B to A.
  Therefore, we can set up the following equations:
  d = 70t1  (distance = speed x time)
  d = 90t2
  We also know that exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  This means that at time t2 - 3, Kevin was 70 miles away from B.
  Therefore, we can set up the following equation:
  70 = 90(t2 - 3)
  Solving for t2, we get:
  t2 = 25/3
  Substituting t2 into the equation d = 90t2, we get:
  d = 750/3 = 250
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 250 miles.
  The answer is C: 270.

  We also know that t1 + t2 = d / 70 + (d - 70) / 90 = (8d - 490) / 630.
  We can set up another equation that relates all these variables: t1 + t2 = (5d + 70) / 63.
  Now we can solve these two equations for d.
  (2d + 110) / 63 = (5d + 70) / 63 - 3
  2d + 110 = 5d + 70 - 189
  4d = 229
  d = 57.25
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 57.25 miles.
  The answer is E: None of the above.

  Kevin turned around and drove at a constant speed of 90 mph from B to A, so the time he took to cover the same distance is also x/90.
  We know that exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  This means that he had driven a total of x - 70 miles when there were 3 hours left.
  We can use this information to set up an equation and solve for x.

Calculation:
  Let's use the formula: distance = rate x time
  Kevin drove x miles from A to B at 70 mph, so the time he took is x/70.
  Kevin drove x miles from B to A at 90 mph, so the time he took is x/90.
  Kevin drove x - 70 miles when there were 3 hours left, so the time he had left is (3 hours).
  We can set up the equation: x/70 + x/90 + 3 = (x - 70)/90
  Multiplying both sides by 630 (the least common multiple of 70 and 90), we get: 9x + 7x + 1890 = 7x - 4900
  Simplifying, we get: 9x + 7x = -4900 - 1890, which is 16x = -6790
  Dividing both sides by 16, we get: x = -424.375
  Since distance cannot be negative, this answer is not possible.
  Therefore, the answer is E: None of the above.

  90 x 3 = 270 miles

  d - 270

  2d
  So, we have the equation:
  d - 270 = 2d
  Solving for d, we get:
  d = 270
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 270 miles.

  Let's write this equation in terms of a, b, c, d, and e.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are "x" employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributed "y" amount of money to raise Rs. 6 lakh.
  Therefore, the equation is: x*y = 6,00,000  --- (1)
  If each employee contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution of each employee is y+60.
  The new total contribution would be 6.24 lakh.
  Therefore, the equation is: x*(y+60) = 6,24,000  --- (2)
  We can solve these two equations to find the value of "x".
  Equation (2) can be simplified to x*y + 60x = 6,24,000
  Substituting the value of x*y from equation (1), we get:
  6,00,000 + 60x = 6,24,000
  60x = 24,000
  x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributes 'x' amount of money.
  The total amount of money raised is equal to the product of the number of employees and the amount of money contributed by each employee.
  From the problem statement, we can form two equations:
    nx = 600000
    n(x+60) = 624000
  We can solve for 'n' by dividing the second equation by the first equation:
    (n(x+60))/nx = 624000/600000
    (x+60)/x = 1.04
    x = 600
  Substituting the value of 'x' in the first equation:
    nx = 600000
    n = 1000
  Therefore, there are 1000 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:

  If each employee contributes equally to raise Rs. 6 lakh, then the contribution of each employee is 6 lakh divided by x.

  We can set up an equation using the above information and solve for x.
  (6.24 lakh) / x = (6 lakh / x) + 60
  Multiplying both sides by x gives:
  6.24 lakh = 6 lakh + 60x
  0.24 lakh = 60x
  x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
  The answer is C: 400.

### Temperature: 4.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the amount received by each nephew be x.
Amount received by each daughter = 4x
Amount received by each son = 5x
Total number of children = 5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11
Total amount = Rs 8600
Therefore, (5*5x) + (4*4x) + (2*x) = 8600
Solving the above equation gives x = 200
Amount received by each daughter = 4x = 4*200 = 800
Therefore, each daughter receives Rs 800.
Action: Answer("E")

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let the number be x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, so his calculation was (7/18)x.
  The actual value of 7/8 of the number is (7/8)x.
  The difference between the student's answer and the actual answer is 770.
  Therefore, (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770.
  Simplifying the equation, we get (35/72)x = 770.
  Solving for x, we get x = (770*72)/35 = 1584.
  Therefore, the number is 1584.
Action: Answer("A")

Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  Let's assume that we travel x quarter-miles after the first quarter-mile.
  The cost of traveling x quarter-miles is 10x cents.
  The total cost of the trip is $8.50.
  Therefore, we can write the equation: 350 cents + 10x cents = 850 cents.
  Solving for x, we get x = 50 quarter-miles.
  Therefore, the total distance traveled is 1 + 50/4 = 13 miles.
  However, we need to subtract the distance traveled in the first quarter-mile.
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel is 13 - 0.25 = 12.75 miles.
  The answer is B: 12.75 miles.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile.
  Therefore, the amount left for additional quarter miles is $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00.

  Therefore, the number of additional quarter miles that can be traveled is $5.00 / $0.10 = 50.
  The total distance traveled is the first quarter-mile plus the additional quarter miles.
  Therefore, the total distance traveled is 1 + 50/4 = 14.75 miles.
  The answer is D: 14.75 miles.

  We can subtract the initial $3.50 from the total amount to get the amount we have left to spend on additional quarter-miles.

  We can divide the remaining amount by the cost of each additional quarter-mile to get the maximum number of additional quarter-miles we can travel.
  $5.00 ÷ $0.10 = 50
  We can add the initial quarter-mile to the maximum number of additional quarter-miles to get the maximum distance we can travel.

  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50 is 13 miles.
